<div id="review_238334963" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/238334963" />
    <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship"><img alt="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1297107033p2/2109885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/238334963?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}" href="/user/show/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship">Literary Ames {Against GR Censorship}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780857531353" href="/book/show/11544503-starters">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of TV's Dollhouse</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=series-abandoned">series-abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=free-read">free-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=1st-in-series">1st-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=dystopian-or-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-or-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2109885-literary-ames-against-gr-censorship?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer238334963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15982100281387273406">Super strong opening chapters with a premise similar to TV’s Dollhouse which although interesting, threw up more questions than answers.<br/><br/><i>Starters</i> shines the spotlight on a section of society which is sometimes overlooked or given the least respect but which will in future be the most powerful: the old. One day there will be fewer young people to support the ever-increasing number of elderly citizens, and here we can see how things could change in their favour.<br/><br/>Starters are under 19 years of age, t</span>
  <span id="freeText15982100281387273406" style="display:none">Super strong opening chapters with a premise similar to TV’s Dollhouse which although interesting, threw up more questions than answers.<br><br><i>Starters</i> shines the spotlight on a section of society which is sometimes overlooked or given the least respect but which will in future be the most powerful: the old. One day there will be fewer young people to support the ever-increasing number of elderly citizens, and here we can see how things could change in their favour.<br><br>Starters are under 19 years of age, those just starting out in life and Enders are the elderly. The generations inbetween have all died after biological warfare prompted the vaccination of the vulnerable –the old and the young, leaving those in the middle to die prolonged and agonizing deaths. <br><br>From the technology available I would guess we’re about 50 years in the future in a post-war America. The reasons for the war aren’t given. All we know is that Pacific Rim countries were involved and that America used an EMP weapon on them and they retaliated with a biologically engineered disease –game, set, match.<br><br>The age gap creates a huge gulf between the Starters and Enders. Old legislation addressing the increasing aging population means anyone under 19 cannot work and the large numbers of unclaimed minors whose family have died are unable to legitimately provide for themselves. Orphanages are basically workhouses with inmates treated as prisoners; no one wants to end up there. Squatting and thieving is how most get by, dodging the child-catching Marshals whenever possible. Adoption or fostering seems non-existent. Enders don’t care about Starters unless they’re family. I find this surprising because many Enders would’ve lost children, relatives. Some may be the last members of their families. Hasn’t loneliness spurred any to seek adoption?<br><br>The story follows Callie, a Starter, who lost her parents to the war. She has no grandparents and is forced to care for her 7-year-old brother by herself with a little help from Michael, a boy who used to live down the street from her pre-war. They’re currently squatting in an abandoned building practically starving. She can’t bear to watch her sick brother lose any more weight so she visits the not so ethical or legal, Prime Destinations, a place which rents out the bodies of teenagers to Enders who pay large sums of money to feel young again. If she does this she’ll have enough cash to pay for a home and medical care for her brother for the next few years. <br><br>For obvious reasons Callie’s reluctant to do this but she has little choice. Unfortunately things don’t go quite to plan, Callie suddenly wakes up in a nightclub instead of the lab and finds out the renter of her body wishes to murder someone. Scared, she pretends she’s her renter to safeguard her payment and attempts to stop her renter from committing this crime which will no doubt lead to her own execution.<br><br>Along the way she encounters other renters taking full advantage of their new temporary bodies and think nothing of stealing the lives of the body’s original owners. They take the old adage ‘Youth is wasted on the young’ to heart. These privileged Enders are selfish and greedy. The predatory gleam in the eyes of those at PD were quite creepy, eyeing up the young like they’re cattle for slaughter, salivating at the thought of inhabiting their supple bodies and smooth, wrinkle-free skin. *shudders*<br><br>These Enders aren’t your average old people. They live to 200 years old and appear to have no health problems due to advances in medicine, odd because not all Enders are rich and the last time I checked medical care wasn’t free in America so how come none of them appear hampered by age. Sure, some have wrinkles (and others get cosmetic surgery) and watery eyes but no problems running or experiencing a full working life.<br><br>Carrie also finds herself spending time with a handsome and rich teen, Blake. Her Prince Charming. Whenever she’s around him the urgency of her predicament, racing-against-time to stop the murder, fades into the background. A day out horse-riding with him and she forgets her responsibilities and starts comparing herself to Cinderella, wondering if the girl from the fairy tale ever considered telling her prince she’s a fraud. I never understood Blake’s appeal considering the over-familiar way he behaves, acting like they’re closer than the strangers they are. And Callie’s ambiguous relationship with Michael –are they more than friends? Even at the end it isn’t clear. Is a love triangle on the horizon?<br><br>Reading about how vaccinating the old and young from something so deadly implies this is the wrong course of action generally. Yes, the elderly are an invaluable source of knowledge, wisdom and experience but in a situation where you have limited resources and a serious biological threat, is protecting the weakest to the detriment of the strong really the right decision to make? In this case it left children without parents, manual labour is carried out by those children because the elderly were either too frail or simply felt they were above such work. <br><br>The plot is interesting if slightly predictable and the characters are quite thin, I didn't feel particularly attached to any of them. I did have some problems understanding the technology either because we’re given names of something but not what it does or because something we all ready have has been rebranded e.g. Z-mail a.k.a. e-mail, Zing a.k.a. text message –took me a bit to figure that one out. The focus of the book is on the very rich and the very poor Starters but we don't get to see those in the middle, nor do we see any poor Enders. The last page was intriguing but I'm not sure if I'll read the sequel for one reason: the possibility of a love triangle. The rest I believe will be developed and improved upon but I can't abide love triangles.<br><br><i>***Many thanks to NetGalley and the publisher for providing me with a copy of this book in return for an honest review.***</i><br><br>__________________________________________________<br><br><br>The tagline: <i>"Your body. Rented out. Used to murder."</i> sold it to me.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363592i/715031.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15982100281387273406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1232710873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1232710873" />
    <a title="Pinky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky"><img alt="Pinky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489855494p2/27523984.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1232710873?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pinky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pinky" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky">Pinky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1232710873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9383555295270743502"> I had mixed feelings about this book. I liked the characters but I wasn't attached to them. The writing style was smooth and nice. Some of the characters thoughts or actions did not make sense. The plot was very different from the usual books I read. This book is really different and for some reason, it is almost similar to the Host.<br/><br/> After the Spore War, when Callie was younger, her parents died. Callie, her brother Tyler, and her friend Micheal have to find a way to survive on the streets. Cal</span>
  <span id="freeText9383555295270743502" style="display:none"> I had mixed feelings about this book. I liked the characters but I wasn't attached to them. The writing style was smooth and nice. Some of the characters thoughts or actions did not make sense. The plot was very different from the usual books I read. This book is really different and for some reason, it is almost similar to the Host.<br /><br /> After the Spore War, when Callie was younger, her parents died. Callie, her brother Tyler, and her friend Micheal have to find a way to survive on the streets. Callie has nothing left but Tyler and Micheal as her family. So her only hope to survive is to go to the Prime Destinations. This is also known as the body bank, where teens rent their bodies to old people called Enders. The Prime Destinations pay teens a great deal of money so Callie had no choice but to rent her body. While the Enders live in a younger body, the teens live in an Ender's body.<br /><br /> The reason I had mixed feelings about this book was because of the decisions Callie made. When Callie met Sara, she wanted to punch Sara's face so they wouldn't pick her. But the Prime Destinations can heal the wounds and also add different chemicals when they do the makeover. It didn't make any sense. I couldn't believe that Callie would leave her brother with a complete stranger. I know that she had no choice, but I would never do that. <br /><br /> One of the reasons why I didn't get too attached to the character was because of the fact that we never saw that much of them. When I was reading about Micheal, he seemed nice but we never saw much of him. Tyler was the only character I was attached to but he wasn't in the book that much either. I had mixed thoughts about Florine and Blake.<br /><br /> This book was really unique and the whole story was really interesting. I felt that it was fast-paced but there were parts of the book where it was going slow. It's not one of my favorite books but I still liked and enjoyed it. This action-packed, dystopian novel was really amazing. I would recommend it to anyone who loved the Host or loves dystopian novels.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>P.S, I haven't been on Goodreads lately because of a huge reading slump!</i>
</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9383555295270743502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_268926096" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268926096" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3085245-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262799010p2/3085245.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268926096?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/3085245-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268926096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6996834442476016262">Starters is another book in the YA Dystopian genre. I thought Starters started out well, but then the story line just had me asking too many questions. There were too many things that I just didn't get. With a lot of the dystopian novels there are certain world-building aspects that may be a little odd or unrealistic that you just have to accept before you can enjoy the novel. The key is whether you can move past it or not. For example, with Matched or Delirium, I find it unlikely that Society w</span>
  <span id="freeText6996834442476016262" style="display:none">Starters is another book in the YA Dystopian genre. I thought Starters started out well, but then the story line just had me asking too many questions. There were too many things that I just didn't get. With a lot of the dystopian novels there are certain world-building aspects that may be a little odd or unrealistic that you just have to accept before you can enjoy the novel. The key is whether you can move past it or not. For example, with Matched or Delirium, I find it unlikely that Society would ever tell you who to marry or not to love. But, assuming you accept that premise as fact and move on, the stories make sense for the most part. With Starters there were just too many things that did not make sense to me. Before I list those, I should probably summarize the premise of the book. During the spore wars, deadly spores were released in the US killing anyone who was not vaccinated. Due to limited supply of the vaccine prior to the war, only the most vulnerable in the population received the vaccine, which was people under 20 and people over 60. It's now been a year after the war and the only consequence seems to be that everyone between the ages of 20 and 60 is dead. Oh, and people live to be 200 is this world. As a result, rich old people pay a lot of money to rent the bodies of young people so that they can do things like go ice skating and go to dance clubs again. So assuming we accept all of that, there was still too much that just didn't fit. Bear with me because this is list is long:<br /><br />Why are there so many unclaimed minors? Think about all the people you know between the ages of 0 and 20. How many of them have a least one living relative over the age of 60 who would claim them (in order to keep the kid from being institutionalized)? Probably most. Now imagine that people live to the age of 200. I just find it hard to believe that there are so many kids without a living relative to vouch for them.<br /><br />There are a lot of teens and grandparents in the story line. The grandparents tend to be about 100 years older than the teens. That implies about 50 years between generations. Therefore most of these teens' parents should be in their 60's and thus would not have died in the spore wars.<br /><br />Why does Callie like Blake? He's extremely boring. "Oh, I feel a special connection to you." There was nothing there, I didn't get it.<br /><br />Why was Blake willing to do that favor for Callie? Let's say someone you just met at club the night before, asks you to drive your Ferrari to the projects to give a "friend" of theirs $3,000 and tells you not to stay long because it's dangerous. Would you do it? Of course not.<br /><br />Why didn't they go to Senator Bohn at the beginning? I failed to see what additional evidence they gained during the course of the book that would aid in taking down Prime Destinations.<br /><br />Before the spore wars killed everyone, people under 20 were not allowed to work since there were so many aging people who needed jobs. Overlooking the fact that a law like that probably wouldn't help, once a quarter of the workforce was removed, wouldn't you quickly repeal that law to try to get some of those young people to take over the jobs of all those dead people? Think about during WWII when so many women went to work while the men were deployed.<br /><br />If people under 20 are not allowed to work, why do all of the young people in the institutions have work detail? Seems pretty contradictory. Slave labor is preventing some old person from getting a legitimate paying job, right?<br /><br />In the beginning of the book, it seems like all people over 60 are selfish, evil human beings. Yet by the end of the book there are a lot of nice, decent people over 60. <br /><br />Why did Callie like Blake again in the end? To me this implied that Callie was lonely and Blake was good looking, so why not? Not to mention the creepiness factor, which I can't explain without giving away too much.<br /><br />I also thought that the character development was lacking. The author tended to tell instead of show - for example, Callie's amazing target-shooting ability. We're told that Callie's father taught her how to shoot when she was less than 13 years old. Apparently during that time she became a sharp-shooter. Three years later after absolutely no practice, she's still an amazing shooter. It felt more like an afterthought than character development. It's convenient to the plot if Callie knows how to use a gun, so let's make her a sharp shooter. If you compare that, say, to Katniss's ability to use a slingshot or bow and arrow in the Hunger Games, it fails miserably. Yes, Katniss's father taught her how to use a bow and arrow, but she slowly perfected her talent over years of using it ever day. It's how she survived and it's a part of who she is. It defined her and it played an important role throughout all of the books. <br /><br />I know this review is quite critical, and it's partially because I think this book will appeal to a lot of people because the dystopian genre is so trendy right now. Despite my rather heavy to list of flaws, I did finish the book. I liked the writing, and the action was good, making it easy to read even when I thought some things were a little far-fetched. Mainly, I think that the plot needed to be a lot tighter.<br /><br />See other reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.thebookclimber.com">www.thebookclimber.com</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6996834442476016262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15965694151279660247"><b>Summary</b><br/><i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11861062.Starters__Starters___1_' title='Starters (Starters, #1) by Lissa Price' rel='nofollow noopener'>Starters</a>
</i> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4902564.Lissa_Price' title='Lissa Price' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lissa Price</a> is an excitingly addictive story! After the Spore War that wiped out everyone not vaccinated (everyone ages 20-60), Callie Woodland, a sixteen-year-old unclaimed orphan, is living in an abandoned office building with her younger brother, Tyler. Life is terrible--running from renegades who would kill her just for a cookie, living in a cold, abandoned office building with no clean water, heat, or food, and hiding from marshals that want to institutionalize them a</span>
  <span id="freeText15965694151279660247" style="display:none"><b>Summary</b><br /><i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11861062.Starters__Starters___1_" title="Starters (Starters, #1) by Lissa Price" rel="nofollow noopener">Starters</a>
</i> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4902564.Lissa_Price" title="Lissa Price" rel="nofollow noopener">Lissa Price</a> is an excitingly addictive story! After the Spore War that wiped out everyone not vaccinated (everyone ages 20-60), Callie Woodland, a sixteen-year-old unclaimed orphan, is living in an abandoned office building with her younger brother, Tyler. Life is terrible--running from renegades who would kill her just for a cookie, living in a cold, abandoned office building with no clean water, heat, or food, and hiding from marshals that want to institutionalize them and the other children. Since her brother is sick, she desperately needs money...so she "donates" her body to a place called Prime Destinations, which is run by an unknown figure known as The Old Man. At Prime, elders (a.k.a. Enders) rent teens' (a.k.a. Starters) bodies! They do that by inserting a chip into the Starters' heads, and each Ender has control over the teenage body that they rent! After giving the teens a makeover, the elders live as the teens while the teens are unconscious in their own bodies. But something went wrong with Callie's chip...and she is able to gain back control over her body for short periods of time! She wakes up to a world of luxury and has a handsome boyfriend. Through the malfunction, Callie uncovers the Old Man's sinister plans! In the meantime, her renter has plans of her own, and forces Callie to help her... Can Callie stop the Enders?<br /><br /><b>About the Author</b><br />Lissa Price is a newcomer who is obviously talented to write such a good book! I literally could not stop reading this story. She is truly talented!! For more information about the author, Lissa Price, you can go to <a href="http://www.lissaprice.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.lissaprice.com</a>. :)<br /><br /><b>My Opinion</b><br />While I was reading the story, I felt like I was watching a movie and I had to find out what happened in the end! The author could have been a bit more descriptive about the characters, but because the story was so good, that didn't matter! The storyline was very thrilling and addictive, (I read the whole eBook at once!) and I think it would work out great as a movie, too! I can't wait to read the next book in the series, <i>Enders</i>! Lissa Price is now officially one of my favorite authors and I can't wait to read more books by her. :)<br /><br />**I received a copy of this eBook for free from Random House Children's Books and NetGalley in exchange for an honest review. I received no other compensation.**<br /><br /><a href="http://reviewsbykristina.blogspot.com/2012/01/starters-by-lissa-price.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Starters Blog Post</a><br /><br /><a href="http://www.KristinaCardoza.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristina Cardoza</a></span>

    <div class="updateActionLinks">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Sn/KwiEU9g9fk5fyC/Jb+3lk9YfC8M4nprS1kDFvPV5wWaMQmko/Z/i4I5P8B1EkrzsSTwx9QED9yvMh/CzPxA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('jc2+bjgIXJ2aJNwnyCLuzz+LdmkmReP/sJwGa2H8+FO369e8g1aV9T0PaEY/1+QQ6dSRoejIbZjr4kDarL8KyQ==')})
  }

A Writer\'s Diary began as a column in a literary journal, but by 1876 Dostoevsky was able to bring it out as a complete monthly publication with himself as an editor, publisher, and sole contributor, suspending work on The Brothers Karamazov to do so.\n \nThe Diary\'s radical format was matched by the extreme range of its contents. In a single frame it incorporated an astonishing variety of material: short stories; humorous sketches; reports on sensational crimes; historical predictions; portraits of famous people; autobiographical pieces; and plans for stories, some of which were never written while others appeared later in the Diary itself. A range of authorial and narrative voices and stances and an elaborate scheme of allusions and cross-references preserve and present Dostoevsky\'s conception of his work as a literary whole.\n \nSelected from the two-volume set, this abridged edition of A Writer\'s Diary appears in a single paperback volume, along with a new condensed introduction by editor Gary Saul <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2019019444662355856">Lissa Price’s debut novel STARTERS is an award-winning, international bestseller published in over thirty countries. Dean Koontz called this YA futuristic thriller “a smart, swift, inventive, altogether gripping story.” The LA Times said it is “Dystopian science-fiction at its best,” and “Readers who have been waiting for a worthy successor to ‘The Hunger Games’ will find it here.” <br/><br/>STARTERS was a </span>
  <span id="freeText2019019444662355856" style="display:none">Lissa Price’s debut novel STARTERS is an award-winning, international bestseller published in over thirty countries. Dean Koontz called this YA futuristic thriller “a smart, swift, inventive, altogether gripping story.” The LA Times said it is “Dystopian science-fiction at its best,” and “Readers who have been waiting for a worthy successor to ‘The Hunger Games’ will find it here.” <br /><br />STARTERS was a Barnes &amp; Noble pick of the month and one of only four debuts on the B&amp;N Best Teen Books of 2012. It was awarded the its Eselsohr for Best YA Book in 2012, selected by a jury of teens in Germany, and was chosen as a top ten favorite book of 2012 by both French and German readers. It won the Crimezone Award for Best YA Thriller and is one of the LAPL's and Chicago Public Library's Best Teen Books of 2012.<br /><br />Starters was chosen for the IRA Reading List and is the only book nominated for both the Florida Teens Read List and the SSYRA Middle School List 2013-14.<br /><br />In Germany, Starters launched a brand-new YA imprint of the established Piper Verlag publisher called IVI. Audiobooks have been recorded in English and German.<br /><br />See the book trailer that played in front of the Hunger Games film in selected theaters in the US and abroad at her site. The release dates for Enders will be announced by the publishers of each country, with some starting in May 2013.<br /><br />If you want to contact Lissa, please do it through her website, fb, twitter or tumblr and not here. She's happy to email you back if you reach out to her that way. She thanks everyone for their support!<br /></span>
